       <article class="content-wrapper wrapper clearfix detail-block-md" id="article-33855">
        <header class="content-header">
         <h1>
          Completely Unrealistic TV Character Has Complex, Multifaceted Personality
         </h1>
        </header>
        <main class="content-body large-thing" data-area="Article Body">
         <div class="content-masthead">
         </div>
         <div class="content-meta small-thing">
          <div>
           <a class="content-type" data-track-action="Meta: Feature Type" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/search?tags=" href="/features/news-in-brief">
            NEWS IN BRIEF
           </a>
           <span class="content-published">
            September 13, 2013
           </span>
          </div>
          <div>
           <span class="content-issue">
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Issue" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/issue/4937/" href="/issue/4937/">
             Vol 49 Issue 37
            </a>
            <span class="bul">
             
            </span>
           </span>
           <span class="content-tags">
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Tags" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/tag/news" href="/tag/news">
             News
            </a>
            <span class="bul">
             
            </span>
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Tags" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/tag/entertainment" href="/tag/entertainment">
             Entertainment
            </a>
            <span class="bul">
             
            </span>
            <a data-track-action="Meta: Tags" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="/tag/tv" href="/tag/tv">
             Tv
            </a>
           </span>
          </div>
          <div class="article-share-tools share-container">
           <div class="share-tools share-widget" data-share-description="NEW YORKAccording to a number of prominent television critics nationwide, the HBO series Boardwalk Empire stretches belief to the breaking point by featuring an incredibly implausible main character who is a complex human being with a layere..." data-share-image="http://i.onionstatic.com/onion/None/16x9/1200.jpg" data-share-redirect-url="http://www.theonion.com/fb-close" data-share-title="Completely Unrealistic TV Character Has Complex, Multifaceted Personality" data-share-url="http://www.theonion.com/r/33855">
            <a class="share-facebook button" data-action="Facebook share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Facebook" href="#" target="_blank" title="Share via Facebook">
             <i class="fa fa-facebook fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
            <a class="share-twitter button" data-action="Twitter share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Twitter" href="#" title="Share via Twitter">
             <i class="fa fa-twitter fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
            <a class="share-mail button" data-action="Email share clicked" data-track-action="Meta: Share" data-track-category="Article" data-track-label="Email" href="#" title="Share via Email">
             <i class="fa fa-envelope fa-fw">
             </i>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="dfp dfp-slot-article-button" data-ad-unit="article-button" data-targeting='{"dfp_pagetype": "article", "dfp_content_id": 33855}'>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="large-thing content-main">
          <div class="content-text">
           <div>
            <p>
             NEW YORKAccording to a number of prominent television critics nationwide, the HBO series
             <i>
              Boardwalk Empire
             </i>
             stretches belief to the breaking point by featuring an incredibly implausible main character who is a complex human being with a layered, ambiguous, and nuanced personality. I honestly want to like Nucky, the main character, but its frankly really hard to swallow this super unrealistic fantasy universe where human beings act with purpose, have complicated thoughts and opinions, are motivated by coherent desires, and are more than just superficial, mindless stereotypes, wrote
             <i>
              Washington Post
             </i>
             TV critic Hank Stuever in a recent column, adding that while individuals in the real world drift thoughtlessly through their entire unexamined lives, the shows incredibly far-fetched protagonist seemed to have a deep inner life, an actual original point of view, and a sense of moral conflict. The whole premise that there are people out there with a full, expressive range of emotions, and a worldview that is willing to see things in more shades than simply black and white, is just completely preposterous. I mean, do the writers seriously expect us to buy this nonsense? Stuever conceded, however, that he found the shows depiction of a bleak, inhospitable universe just about right on the money.
            </p>
           </div>
          </div>

           <div class="share-container">
